Question input triggers first retrieval (Hop 1) using ColBERTv2 to fetch k=7 passages\n2. Retrieved passages are summarized via chain-of-thought prompting\n3. A second query is generated from the question and first summary (Hop 2)\n4. Second retrieval fetches additional passages based on the refined query\n5. Second set of passages is summarized with context from the first summary\n6. Final answer is generated using both summaries and the original question\n\n**Metric**: The system optimizes for `exact_match_metric` (dspy.evaluate.answer_exact_match), which measures whether the generated answer exactly matches the gold answer string from the HotpotQA dataset."}

Iteration 1: Proposed new text for program.create_query_hop2.predict: Task Description: 

You will be provided with two fields as input: `question` and `summary_1`. Your task is to produce a `query` output field that serves as an effective, targeted search query to verify or retrieve relevant information to answer the question, ideally incorporating the key elements from both the `question` and the `summary_1`. 

The inputs:

- `question`: A natural language question or prompt that asks for a specific fact, name, date, or confirmation.
- `summary_1`: A concise factual statement or answer snippet related to the question, often directly providing the correct answer or relevant details.

Your output:

- `query`: A carefully constructed search query (usually a short phrase or sentence) designed to yield authoritative or confirming sources when searched in a knowledge base or search engine. The query should reflect the core entities, roles, dates, or relationships in the question together with the content in the summary. The query can include names, titles, dates, keywords, and disambiguating details from both inputs.

Guidelines and considerations based on the examples and feedback:

1. **Use concise, keyword-rich queries:**  
   Include relevant proper nouns, dates, titles, and key descriptors from both the question and summary. Avoid mere verbatim repetition of summary answers unless they alone serve as effective queries (e.g., a clear proper noun answer).

2. **Clarify and disambiguate when needed:**  
   If the question asks for a relationship or comparison (e.g., "Who was born first?"), build a comparative query mentioning both subjects and the respective relevant facts (birth dates, events). If the summary gives multiple relevant pieces of info (e.g., names, dates), include those.

3. **Do not return a declarative sentence as the query:**  
   Avoid providing the answer statement itself as a query (e.g., avoid queries that read like a full sentence or a confirmed fact). Instead, create a search query that someone could use to find a source to verify that fact. For example, do not simply return "Both Mark Steyn and Tucker Carlson are conservative commentators." Instead, transform it into "Mark Steyn Tucker Carlson political views conservative commentators."

4. **Address questions that involve multiple entities or comparisons:**  
   When the question involves two or more persons, shows, or concepts, construct a query mentioning all relevant entities and their linkage (e.g., "Joe Tracini Boomerang show 2000", "Shaun Ryder birth date 1962 Ed Roland birth date 1963").

5. **Include key contextual identifiers:**  
   For entities with potential ambiguity, include disambiguating terms such as birth dates, locations, affiliations, or specific episode names/dates, e.g., "The Simpsons January 21, 1990 Waylon Smithers Homer promoted Nuclear Safety Inspector".

6. **Avoid adding unnecessary filler or overly broad terms:**  
   Keep the query focused and targeted for the question and summary, avoiding generic or broad terms that don’t aid retrieval.

7. **When the summary includes proper titles or names, use them accurately with any necessary punctuation or quotes to preserve clarity in the query:**  
   This also applies to cases of TV shows, book titles, or named entities, e.g., `"Ren & Stimpy Adult Party Cartoon" John Kricfalusi APM Music` rather than fragmentary or ambiguous forms.

8. **No need to restate the 'reasoning' or elaborate the answer within the 'query' field.**  
   The query should be a short search phrase, not a textual explanation.

9. **When the question expects a yes/no answer or a single label (e.g., political orientation, nationality):**  
   Construct a query that would help verify this (e.g., include the names and relevant descriptors like "Mark Steyn and Tucker Carlson political views" rather than returning "Both are conservative commentators").

10. **Integration of both entities and topical keywords:**
    Queries should reflect both question intent and the confirming summary to maximize precision and recall in search.

In summary, your goal is to convert the combination of a question and a factual summary answer into a precise search query string that could be used to confirm or find authoritative information addressing the question.

Example schema:

Input:  
- question: *[some question]*  
- summary_1: *[concise factual content related to the question]*  

Output:  
- query: *[targeted, concise keyword query including relevant names, dates, titles, and descriptors from both inputs]*

Iteration 3: Proposed new text for create_query_hop2.predict: Given two input fields, `question` and `context`, your task is to produce a precise, concise `query` that will efficiently retrieve or confirm the specific answer to the question by focusing on key entities, facts, or relationships described in the `context`.

Detailed task description and guidance:

1. **Input format:**
   - `question`: a natural language question asking for specific information, typically about a named entity (person, place, event, film, award, year, etc.).
   - `context`: one or multiple paragraphs containing relevant information extracted from documents or knowledge bases, often explicitly containing the answer or strongly hinting at it.

2. **Output requirement:**
   - Produce a single field `query` that is a succinct search string or natural language question that can be used to confirm or find the answer to the original question.
   - The `query` should be focused on the essential entity/fact relationship that answers the question and should ideally include key names, dates, or titles mentioned in the `context` relevant to the question.
   - Avoid including unnecessary information or overly long explanations. The query should be clear, targeted, and effective for retrieving a correct answer.
   
3. **Reasoning behind query formulation:**
   - Identify the main entities involved (e.g., a person, film, event).
   - Determine the key fact or attribute the question requests (e.g., year of birth, director’s name, award received).
   - Use the context to spot the exact information needed to resolve the question.
   - Formulate the query around those key components, including titles, names, dates, and other identifiers to disambiguate.
   - In cases where the context fully answers the question, the query may be a straightforward retrieval or confirmation query involving the key entity.

4. **Domain-specific considerations:**
   - When the question references awards, actors, directors, films, or institutions, highlight the exact name/title and attribute (e.g., "director of film X", "birth year of singer Y").
   - If the question involves comparison (e.g., enrollment numbers, election results), include both entities and the comparative factor in the query.
   - When the question requires identification of relationships (e.g., who founded a group, who created a sitcom), the query should frame that link explicitly.
   - Use canonical, full forms of names or titles when possible to reduce ambiguity.
   - For numeric or date questions, include the subject entity and the attribute requested (e.g., "birth date of X," "year Y changed name").

5. **Examples of effective queries:**
   - To find who directed a particular film:  
     “Who directed [Film Name]?”
   
   - To find the birth year of a person referenced:  
     “When was [Person’s Full Name] born?”
   
   - To identify an election outcome involving named candidates:  
     “Who did [Winner’s Name] beat in the [Year] [Election Name]?”
   
   - To verify confirmation of a relationship or fact stated in context:  
     “[Entity A] and [Entity B] relation or connection”

6. **Avoid:**
   - Queries that only restate the answer (unless confirming a named entity as the core query is intended).
   - Verbose queries that are not directly focused on the essential information.
   - Queries that confuse multiple entities or blur the focus from what the question specifically asks.

**Summary:**  
Your goal is to convert a given `question` and supporting `context` into an effective, minimal, and targeted `query` that will help retrieve or verify the precise answer. Use key entity names, dates, attributes, and relationships surfaced in the context, crafting a clear and focused question or search phrase optimized for factual lookup.

Iteration 5: Proposed new text for program.summarize1.predict: Task Description:
Given two input fields, `question` (a natural language query) and `passages` (a list of text passages each containing factual information potentially related to the question), your task is to generate an accurate, concise, direct, and contextually supported `summary` that answers the question based solely on the content present in the passages.

Detailed Task Requirements and Domain-Specific Guidelines:

1. **Input Format**:
   - `question`: A natural language question, which may seek a specific fact, date, name, explanation, or confirmation.
   - `passages`: A list of one or more text passages, each containing relevant factual information, often including entities (people, places, works, events), dates, and domain-specific details.

2. **Output Format**:
   - `summary`: A brief, precise answer to the question, extracted and synthesized from the passages.
   - The summary should be a direct answer (e.g., a year, a name, "yes" or "no", a phrase) rather than a lengthy explanation or restatement unless the question demands clarification.
   - When ambiguity exists in the question or multiple relevant facts are present, provide a clear, focused, and unambiguous answer.

3. **Reasoning and Information Extraction**:
   - Identify key entities and their relationships relevant to the question within the passages.
   - Use explicit statements from the passages to support the answer.
   - Do not rely on information not contained or clearly inferable from the passages.
   - Recognize domain-specific terminology and conventions:
       - For historical/political questions, terms like "Papal States" denote territories under pope’s rule in Italy before 1870.
       - For media and entertainment, recognize roles (actors, directors, dancers, choreographers, judges) and their associations with shows or films.
       - For music, identify band names, song titles, album release years, awards, and how these relate to the question.
       - For sports, link players with their teams and home stadiums or records.
       - For scientific or technical topics (e.g., space, kickboxing records), understand specific roles or records as stated in the passages.
   
4. **Domain-Specific Knowledge Embedded in Passages** (should be leveraged for accurate answers):
   - Recognize that composers can be linked to collaborators by birth year or other familial ties.
   - TV shows may have hosts distinct from regular participants; being a "professional dancer" is not the same as being a "judge."
   - The lowest point or terminus of a river can be a location where the river’s water evaporates or ends (e.g., "Humboldt Sink").
   - Recorded songs and albums have precise release years and associations, often relevant to their inclusion in soundtracks or films.
   - Literary and artistic works may have differing numbers of acts or versions, and character names and roles in soap operas or TV shows often cross-reference actor identities.
   - Historical territories have official names covering specific time frames.
   - Legal or political roles are linked with specific places and historical periods.
   - Sports venues correspond to universities or professional teams during the stated time periods.
   - Factual disputes or verification questions (such as "Are both X and Y astronauts?") require checking definitions or descriptions precisely.

5. **Common Pitfalls to Avoid**:
   - Do not guess or supply answers not explicitly stated or clearly inferable from the passages.
   - Avoid confusing similar names (e.g., individuals with the same surname but different professions).
   - Distinguish between different roles within entertainment (e.g., judge vs dancer vs host).
   - Avoid misattributing quotes or data points to unrelated passages.
   - Answer in the format and specificity expected by the question, e.g., "yes"/"no" rather than explaining unless clarification is required.
   - For questions asking "What show..." or "What song..." responses should be the title or proper name only.

6. **Generalized Approach**:
    - Read the question carefully, identifying the key information needed.
    - Scan the passages to extract relevant facts.
    - Cross-reference multiple passages if needed to clarify relationships or confirm facts.
    - Formulate a concise answer directly addressing the question.
    - When the question asks for a "yes" or "no", provide exactly that unless otherwise specified.
    - If the answer requires a name or title, answer with the recognized proper noun as given in the passages.
    - If the answer involves a date or year, provide it in its simplest form (e.g., "1899", "November 16, 2012").
    - When incomplete or ambiguous information appears in passages, do not supplement with external knowledge unless no passage contains the answer and you explicitly note this in the summary (rare, and only when absolutely certain).

Summary:  
Extract and synthesize factual information from provided text passages to generate a brief, accurate, and contextually supported answer directly addressing the natural language question, using domain-relevant knowledge embedded in the passages and adhering strictly to content within the input data.

Iteration 7: Proposed new text for extract_answer.predict: Task: Extract the exact short factoid answer to the given question from the provided passages.

Input format:
- A question presented as a concise query.
- One or more passages that contain relevant factual information pertaining to the question.

Output:
- Provide a precise, concise answer phrase or term that directly and exactly answers the question.
- The answer must be explicitly supported by the information within the passages without adding inference beyond the text.
- The answer should be as specific and minimal as possible (typically named entities, dates, places, titles, or keywords).
- Avoid abbreviations or expanded explanations unless explicitly part of the factoid.
- If multiple passages provide the answer, consolidate support but provide one answer only.
- Answers should match the expected answer format evident from passages and question type (e.g., a name, a date, a location, a title).
- Case and formatting should follow the passages' usage (e.g., proper nouns capitalized).

Key considerations and domain-specific nuances:
- Individuals may have formal, full names; include full names if provided and relevant (e.g., "Sir Chandrasekhara Venkata Raman" rather than just "C.V. Raman") unless the question dictates otherwise.
- When an event is described with a phrase (e.g., "presidential election of 1924"), mirror the terminologies found in passages.
- For temporal answers, provide full date if available and relevant, or year/year range as the question demands.
- Map references correctly — for example, if a question references "the first naval recipient of the Medal of Honor," ensure the location or facts linked to that exact individual are delivered.
- In yes/no questions, provide only "yes" or "no," not elaborate explanations.
- When answering “who” questions involving hire or roles, provide the person's name exactly as found in the passages.
- For things such as awards, use the exact award name as given in the passage, including precise titles like "BAFTA TV Award".
- When addressing geographic or organizational entities, provide the full form if passage text presents it fully (e.g., "Southern California," "New South Wales, Australia").
- For compound or multi-word answers (e.g., titles of works, organizations), maintain the exact phrasing and proper punctuation.
- When the question references relationships (e.g., familial relationships, predecessor/successor), the answer should specifically highlight the queried entity (e.g., name of the predecessor or full proper designation).
- Where multiple variants exist (e.g., different people with similar names), use context to identify the accurate entity (e.g., "Abraham Lincoln" rather than just "Lincoln" if specified in passages).
- For answers involving artistic or creative works (songs, albums, films, games), provide the exact title in quotes or as is presented in the passages.
- For answers about precise definitions or origin (e.g., architectural styles), use the exact phrase as in passages.
- For numeric or ordinal answers (e.g., "35th quadrennial presidential election"), provide the accepted label or event matching that ordinal from the text.

Reasoning approach:
- Identify the entity (person, place, event, work, award) around whom the question is focused.
- Search passages for direct mentions linking that entity to a fact answering the question.
- Correlate passages that provide complementary details to triangulate an explicit answer.
- Ensure that the answer is not generalized or vague; it must be precisely and explicitly given in the passages.
- Confirm the answer's correctness by verifying it aligns with the passage(s) content and matches expected answer formats.

Avoid:
- Adding inferred or implicit information not explicitly stated in the passages.
- Providing explanations, reasoning steps, or extra commentary in the final answer (reasoning may be included in intermediate steps but the final answer must be just the factoid).
- Paraphrasing or loosely summarizing; the answer must be exact short factual information derived from the passages.

Summary:
Given a question and supporting passages, output the exact short factoid found in the passages that directly answers the question, respecting formal names, precise dates, titles, and facts as presented, and do so succinctly and accurately.

Iteration 9: Proposed new text for create_query_hop2.predict: Given input fields:

- `question`: a natural language question possibly referencing people, works, events, or entities  
- `passages`: a list of textual passages extracted from various sources, each containing factual information relevant to the question  

Your task is to produce the field:

- `query`: a concise and targeted search query that captures the key entities and relationships necessary to answer the question, based on the provided passages  

Detailed guidance and domain-specific insights:  

1. **Purpose of the Query**:  
   The query should be optimized to retrieve information that directly supports answering the question, ideally reflecting the minimal, relevant set of keywords or phrases that isolate the critical facts found or hinted at within the passages.  

2. **Use of Passages**:  
   - Analyze the passages carefully to identify which ones contain exact or partial answers or crucial information to resolve ambiguities in the question.  
   - Use unique identifiers (names, titles, specific descriptors, phrases in quotes) pulled from the passages to form the search query.  
   - Avoid general or overly broad keywords; prefer precise terms (e.g., full names, specific event names, dates, quoted phrases).  

3. **Handling Entity Disambiguation**:  
   - If multiple entities or individuals are involved (e.g., two people mentioned in the question), ensure the query includes both names or distinguishing details to clarify the context.  
   - When the question involves comparison or timeline, the query should reflect these relational aspects (e.g., “birth date comparison”, “defeated whom in X election”).  

4. **Inclusion of Contextual Clues from Question and Passages**:  
   - Extract clues such as:  
     - Roles or occupations (e.g., actor, musician, film director)  
     - Specific works (e.g., film titles, song names, albums)  
     - Dates or events (e.g., election years, birth dates, festival premieres)  
     - Quotes or unique nicknames  
   - Use these to create queries that focus on the distinguishing attributes relevant to the question.  

5. **Query Format and Style**:  
   - Prefer natural-language-like queries but with focused keyword phrases and significant quoted strings (e.g., "Inked" "outsiders' insider" "like Vice").  
   - Use conjunctions or connective words sparingly, only if critical for disambiguation.  
   - Keep the query succinct yet comprehensive enough to narrow down relevant sources.  

6. **Inferring Missing or Implicit Details**:  
   - When the question implies knowledge beyond direct statements (e.g., “What tribe was American Horse part of?”), base the query on specific alternative names or linguistic/ethnic clues presented in passages (e.g., “American Horse Oglala Lakota”).  
   - If a question asks for a relationship or role (e.g., “what role did X play in Y”), frame the query accordingly with proper nouns and role keywords.  

7. **Examples of Good Queries Derived from Passages and Questions**:  
   - Using names + role + production: `"Bradley Walsh" "Coronation Street" role`  
   - Using relationship + events + entity names: `Edward Timpson defeated Tamsin Dunwoody Crewe and Nantwich by-election`  
   - Using work + event + person: `Bedevilled 2010 premiere Cannes Film Festival`  
   - Using dual names + nationality or team: `Arnór Guðjohnsen Eiður Guðjohnsen national team country`  
   - Using a known phrase or unique quote: `Inked "outsiders' insider" "like Vice"`  

8. **Avoiding Common Pitfalls**:  
   - Do not simply restate the question verbatim as the query; the query must leverage passage evidence to highlight key terms.  
   - Avoid queries that are too vague or only partially related to the question.  
   - Avoid including irrelevant names or details not supported by passages.  
   - When a passage strongly supports a single inference, prioritize referencing that inference in the query.  

By following the above, your queries will effectively pinpoint the necessary data to answer diverse factual questions given source passages.

Guidelines:

1. The question may require identifying a person, date, place, organization, or other specific entity mentioned in the passages.

2. Base the answer solely on the information explicitly stated in the passages.

3. If multiple passages discuss the same entity or fact, synthesize them to find the most accurate and complete form of the answer (e.g., use full names where available rather than partial or informal names).

4. If the question asks for a yes/no answer or a categorical confirmation, respond with a simple "yes" or "no" (in lowercase).

5. Responses should avoid restating the question or adding context; reply only with the shortest fully correct answer.

6. When answering "Who" or "What" questions about leadership, origin, or roles, provide the full, formal names or titles as given in the text unless a shorter known form is clearly unambiguous.

7. For questions about dates or years, provide the date or year as explicitly given in the passages.

8. When the question involves comparison (e.g., "Which was formed more recently?"), provide the shorter entity name or label that exactly answers the comparative query.

By following these rules, extract the shortest accurate answer from the given passages to precisely satisfy the factoid question.

- Extract the answer exactly as stated in the passages without paraphrasing or adding any additional information.
- The answer should be a short factoid, typically a name, date, place, numerical value, title, or specific term, as appropriate based on the question.
- When the passages contain multiple relevant aliases or formal versions of a name, use the form with the most complete, formal, or authoritative presentation, including middle names or honorifics if provided.
- Use the exact terminology as given in the passages to match the expected answer format (e.g., "Reed Elsevier" not "RELX Group", "the 27th Regiment of Foot" not just "the 27th").

- If the question asks for a yes/no answer, respond simply with "yes" or "no" (lowercase), unless the passages provide a direct explicit statement; do not add explanations or qualifying statements.
- If the question involves numeric values (dates, population, monetary amounts), extract the exact number or value, including units and currency symbols if present, as specified.
- For questions involving named entities associated with titles, roles, or relationships, extract the full proper name as stated.
- Your answer must be fully supported by the passages provided, and the reasoning step is for your own use—it need not be output.

Iteration 17: Proposed new text for extract_answer.predict: Task Description:

You will be given a question along with multiple passages containing factual information relevant to the question. Your task is to extract a precise, concise, and exact short factoid answer from the passages that directly answers the question.

Input Format:

- The input includes a question labeled "question" that asks for a specific fact or piece of information.
- The input also includes one or more passages labeled "passages" that contain factual, encyclopedic, or structured information, some of which may explicitly answer the question.
- Passages may contain multiple entries on related or unrelated topics. Your focus is to find the exact fact that answers the question.

Task Requirements:

1. Exact Short Factoid Answer:
   - Extract the shortest, exact phrase or term from the passages that directly answers the question.
   - Avoid adding explanatory text, justification, or reasoning in the final answer output.
   - The answer often corresponds to a proper noun, date, location, name, classification, or a simple "yes"/"no."
   - Use the answer exactly as it appears in the passage unless minor normalization (e.g., removing parentheses explaining acronyms) is needed for clarity.
  
2. Use Only Passage Information:
   - Your answer should be based solely on the information present in the provided passages.
   - Do not add or infer information beyond what is explicitly or clearly stated in the passages.

3. Reasoning Process (Optional in Explanations):
   - When generating intermediate reasoning or explanations (if requested or useful), use direct quotations or concrete references from passages.
   - Show clear evidence from passages that supports the answer.

4. Answer Formatting:
   - Provide the final answer as a concise, standalone phrase or term.
   - For Boolean questions, respond with "yes" or "no" in lowercase.
   - When a person's full name is specified in the passage, provide the full name if the question implies formality or specificity; otherwise, the commonly used name is acceptable.
   - For dates or years, provide the numerical year(s) exactly as given.
   - For named entities, titles, or organizations, provide them using the exact wording from the passage.

5. Precision In Ambiguous Cases:
   - If passages provide multiple relevant pieces of information, choose the one most directly answering the question.
   - Avoid answering with combined, comparative, or summarized statements unless specifically requested.
  
6. Special Cases:
   - If the question asks for a confirmation (e.g., "Are both...") answer with "yes" or "no" only.
   - If a question asks for previous or former names, provide the exact previous name mentioned.
   - If the question involves numeric counts or ordinalities (e.g., "twelfth annual"), provide the numeric ordinal as stated.
   - For geographic questions regarding locations or origins, provide the exact place name attested in passages.

7. Common Pitfalls to Avoid:
   - Do not answer with multiple clauses or sentences summarizing the passage—only provide the short factoid answer.
   - Avoid paraphrasing that changes the identity of the fact.
   - Avoid providing superfluous information like reasoning or context unless specifically asked.

Generalizable Strategy:

- Identify the relevant passage(s) by matching keywords and named entities in the question to titles or content in the passages.
- Locate the explicit statement(s) in the passage that directly answer the question.
- Extract the exact phrase or fact that corresponds to the query.
- For disambiguation questions (e.g., comparing two entities), ensure that the answer clearly reflects the factual relationship (yes/no or numeric).
- Handle named individuals according to passage naming conventions and question specificity.

Examples include extracting:

- Names of people, organizations, awards, and titles exactly as given.
- Dates or years of founding or events.
- Locations or venues named in the passages.
- Numerical facts such as counts, rankings, or order.
- Affirmative or negative confirmation for yes/no questions.

Your response should be succinct, precise, and factual, adhering strictly to the above guidelines.

Iteration 19: Proposed new text for create_query_hop2.predict: Given two input fields: 
- `question`: A natural language question seeking a specific factual answer.  
- `passages`: A list of text excerpts extracted from different sources, each potentially containing information relevant to the question.

Your task is to produce a single output field:  
- `query`: a concise, targeted search query or reformulated question string that would help retrieve the relevant factual answer from the passages or from external sources.

Key details and guidelines for producing the `query`:

1. **Extract and clarify key entities and concepts from the `question`** that direct the answer (e.g., names, dates, titles, events, people, organizations).

2. **Leverage information found in the `passages` to enrich or disambiguate the query:**  
   - Identify relevant entities referenced explicitly in the passages that connect to the question (e.g., if a question references a character and passages identify the associated TV series, include that in the query).  
   - If the passages reveal a commonly known or proper noun related to the question (e.g., a person's full name, exact title of a book, film, or song), include that in the query to make it more precise.  
   - Use factual and canonical information gleaned from the passages that could improve the specificity of the query rather than repeating vague or incomplete terms.

3. **Focus the query on retrieving a specific fact or direct answer related to the question:**  
   - Include relevant keywords such as persons, dates, titles, or relationships discovered from both the question and passages.  
   - When the question compares or relates two or more entities (e.g., “Who passed away first?” or “Are persons X and Y in the same category?”), the query should explicitly mention these entities and the relationship in question.

4. **When passages do not explicitly provide the direct answer, use a well-structured external search style query** that reflects the core of the question combined with insights from the passages (e.g., search for "Person A + attribute B" or "Event name + date + detail").

5. **Queries should be concise, clear, and contain only key words/phrases or short sentences optimized for effective retrieval** of targeted information, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or ambiguity.

6. **When multiple entities are referenced in the question, and the passages clarify their relationship or identity, include them both in the query.**

7. **Queries can include quoted phrases when aiming to capture exact phrases or titles as seen in passages.**

8. **Do not provide answers or explanations in the `query` field; the goal is to make the best possible retrieval query based on the question and supplied passages.**

In summary, your role is to synthesize a fact-focused and passage-informed direct search query from a combination of the natural language question and the evidential content provided, to target precise factual information for answering the question.

Iteration 21: Proposed new text for rerank.predict: Given a question and a passage, determine how relevant the passage is for answering the question. The passage may or may not contain information that directly answers the question; it may be partially related, tangentially related, or completely irrelevant.

You must produce:

1. A **relevance score** reflecting how well the passage answers or helps answer the question, on a scale from 0 to 10, where:  
   - 0 means the passage is completely irrelevant and contains no useful information related to the question.  
   - 10 means the passage fully and directly answers the question with explicit facts.

2. **Reasoning:** Provide a detailed reasoning statement explaining how the passage's content relates to the question, including any implicit or explicit connections, such as naming key entities, dates, places, or other factual details relevant to the question.

3. **Explanation:** A concise summary justifying the assigned relevance score by referencing the presence, absence, or indirectness of facts in the passage with respect to the question.

Additional important guidelines:

- The question often requires specific factual information involving named entities (people, places, titles, awards, dates, products, roles, etc.). Confirm the presence of these exact or clearly linked entities or facts in the passage when deciding relevance.

- When the passage partially covers the topic or mentions entities related but not the precise answer (e.g., mentions one possible answer option but not all aspects), assign a low to moderate score reflecting partial relevance.

- If the passage only tangentially relates (for example, shares broad thematic or contextual connection, such as the same geographical region or general category), assign a very low but nonzero score.

- If the passage is about a different person, concept, or topic entirely, assign zero.

- The presence of a keyword or name alone is not sufficient for a high score unless it answers the question or provides explicit relevant facts.

- The passage may provide information that is relevant only if a particular assumption is true (e.g., an actress named in passage matches a role in the question). In such cases, if the assumption is reasonable but not explicitly confirmed, assign a moderate to high score, but explain the uncertainty.

- The focus is on factual content that answers the question, rather than general background or unrelated biography.

- The passage may contain dates, titles, awards, roles, places, or other specific factual data that directly answers or supports the question.

- Use knowledge of common domain-specific entities such as film cast, sports teams, song titles, awards, military units, geographical regions, and their relationships when assessing relevance.

The final output must be structured as follows:

```
### reasoning  
<your detailed reasoning on relevance and content matching>  

### relevance_score

Iteration 22: Proposed new text for rerank.predict: Given a question and a passage, determine how relevant the passage is for answering the question. The passage may or may not contain information that directly answers the question; it may be partially related, tangentially related, or completely irrelevant.

You must produce:

1. A **relevance score** reflecting how well the passage answers or helps answer the question, on a scale from 0 to 10, where:  
   - 0 means the passage is completely irrelevant and contains no useful information related to the question.  
   - 10 means the passage fully and directly answers the question with explicit facts.

2. **Reasoning:** Provide a detailed reasoning statement explaining how the passage's content relates to the question, including any implicit or explicit connections, such as naming key entities, dates, places, or other factual details relevant to the question.

3. **Explanation:** A concise summary justifying the assigned relevance score by referencing the presence, absence, or indirectness of facts in the passage with respect to the question.

Additional important guidelines:

- The question often requires specific factual information involving named entities (people, places, titles, awards, dates, products, roles, etc.). Confirm the presence of these exact or clearly linked entities or facts in the passage when deciding relevance.

- When the passage partially covers the topic or mentions entities related but not the precise answer (e.g., mentions one possible answer option but not all aspects), assign a low to moderate score reflecting partial relevance.

- If the passage only tangentially relates (for example, shares broad thematic or contextual connection, such as the same geographical region or general category), assign a very low but nonzero score.

- If the passage is about a different person, concept, or topic entirely, assign zero.

- The presence of a keyword or name alone is not sufficient for a high score unless it answers the question or provides explicit relevant facts.

- The passage may provide information that is relevant only if a particular assumption is true (e.g., an actress named in passage matches a role in the question). In such cases, if the assumption is reasonable but not explicitly confirmed, assign a moderate to high score, but explain the uncertainty.

- The focus is on factual content that answers the question, rather than general background or unrelated biography.

- The passage may contain dates, titles, awards, roles, places, or other specific factual data that directly answers or supports the question.

- Use knowledge of common domain-specific entities such as film cast, sports teams, song titles, awards, military units, geographical regions, and their relationships when assessing relevance.

The final output must be structured as follows:

```
### reasoning  
<your detailed reasoning on relevance and content matching>  

### relevance_score  
<integer score from 0 to 10>  

### explanation  
<concise justification for the score, referencing content/non-content of passage>

Iteration 23: Proposed new text for summarize2.predict: Task Description:

You will be given three textual fields as input:  
- `question`: A natural language question often requiring a concise factual answer.  
- `context`: A short phrase or sentence that provides a direct concise answer or key information relevant to the question.  
- `passages`: A list of longer textual excerpts (such as encyclopedia entries, biography snippets, or descriptive paragraphs) containing detailed background information which may include evidence or support for the answer.

Your task is to produce a `summary` field that directly answers the question as succinctly and clearly as possible, grounded in the provided `context` and supported by evidence from the `passages`.

Key requirements and best practices based on domain-specific observations:  

1. **Answer Precision and Conciseness:**  
   - Your summary should directly answer the question with the minimal necessary information.  
   - Avoid verbosity or inclusion of irrelevant background details unless essential for clarity.  
   - Do not restate the question or context verbatim unless it is the best concise answer.

2. **Evidence-Backed Answers:**  
   - Base your summary on the factual information explicitly supported in the `context` and `passages`.  
   - When reasoning or disambiguating, verify that the `context` answer is confirmed by at least one passage that includes clear, relevant supporting facts or identifiers about the person, place, object, event, or concept.  
   - Your reasoning and final summary should reflect alignment between the succinct context and the more detailed passages.

3. **Handling Names and Titles:**  
   - When answering about people, include full formal names or the most common recognized version, unless brevity or directness is called for.  
   - When the question asks for nationality, species, category, or type, provide concise categorical terms (e.g., "American", "Indian physicist", "flowering plants").  
   - If an official or formal name is required (e.g., of an institution or entity), use the correct full official name as supported by the passages.

4. **Disambiguation and Clarity:**  
   - If multiple terms or possibilities are mentioned, clarify which term or entity matches the question by linking the context and passages.  
   - If necessary, clarify alternative or related names (e.g., stage names, birth names) but keep focus on the main answer to the question.

5. **Formatting and Style:**  
   - Use simple declarative sentences or clear noun phrases.  
   - Avoid unnecessary punctuation or elaboration beyond answering the question.  
   - Properly capitalize names and formal nouns.

6. **General Strategy:**  
   - Identify the factual answer in the `context` first.  
   - Find passages that explicitly or implicitly confirm or provide details about the answer.  
   - Cross-check the entities in the passages with the question to rule out ambiguity.  
   - Summarize the confirmed answer clearly and succinctly.

Examples of task domains include but are not limited to:  
- Identifying nationality or profession of persons named.  
- Naming originating countries or teams for sportspeople.  
- Identifying the full proper name of organizations, institutions, or events.  
- Confirming categorizations or classifications (e.g., dog breeds, plant genera).  
- Verifying biographical facts such as birth names, dates, or historical details.  
- Specifying concise answers to questions about television shows, video games, or cultural items tied to specific people.

This task aims at generating a short, precise, and supported factual answer that could be used as an authoritative summary or direct answer snippet.

Your output should be a single field `summary` containing that final answer.
